=== INTERPRETATION ===
FRÉCHET JUMP TESTS ON I-O MATRICES:
- Tests whether full I-O network structure changes discontinuously at threshold
- Uses 'covariance' metric space with Frobenius distance for matrix comparison
- Direct Requirements (A): Tests changes in immediate sectoral dependencies
- Leontief Inverse (L): Tests changes in total economic multiplier structure
- P-values < 0.05 indicate significant structural breaks in production networks

ALTERNATIVE NETWORK APPROACH:
- Could convert I-O flows to graph Laplacians (set alternative section to TRUE)
- Treats sectors as nodes, I-O flows as edge weights
- Uses 'network' metric space designed for graph Laplacians
- Different economic interpretation: network connectivity vs flow intensities

SCALAR RDD RESULTS:
- Standard RDD on derived network measures and complexity indices
- Positive coefficients = higher values above high-income threshold
- Focus on results with p-values < 0.05 for statistical significance

ECONOMIC INTERPRETATION:
- Upstream centrality: Average intensity of inputs provided to other sectors
- Manufacturing intensity: Within-manufacturing sector linkage density
- Economic complexity: Sophistication of production capabilities
- Multiplier effects: Economy-wide impact of demand shocks via Leontief inverse

KEY TECHNICAL NOTES:
- I-O matrices ≠ Graph Laplacians (different mathematical properties)
- A matrices: Non-negative, row sums < 1, represent input coefficients
- L matrices: Diagonal > 1, represent total economic multipliers
- Graph Laplacians: Row sums = 0, off-diagonal ≤ 0, represent network structure

=== NETWORK STRUCTURE ANALYSIS ===
Average non-zero coefficient (below threshold): 0.0739

=== INTERPRETATION ===
FRÉCHET JUMP TESTS ON I-O MATRICES:
- Tests whether full I-O network structure changes discontinuously at threshold
- Uses 'covariance' metric space with Frobenius distance for matrix comparison
- Direct Requirements (A): Tests changes in immediate sectoral dependencies
- Leontief Inverse (L): Tests changes in total economic multiplier structure
- P-values < 0.05 indicate significant structural breaks in production networks

ALTERNATIVE NETWORK APPROACH:
- Could convert I-O flows to graph Laplacians (set alternative section to TRUE)
- Treats sectors as nodes, I-O flows as edge weights
- Uses 'network' metric space designed for graph Laplacians
- Different economic interpretation: network connectivity vs flow intensities

SCALAR RDD RESULTS:
- Standard RDD on derived network measures and complexity indices
- Positive coefficients = higher values above high-income threshold
- Focus on results with p-values < 0.05 for statistical significance

ECONOMIC INTERPRETATION:
- Upstream centrality: Average intensity of inputs provided to other sectors
- Manufacturing intensity: Within-manufacturing sector linkage density
- Economic complexity: Sophistication of production capabilities
- Multiplier effects: Economy-wide impact of demand shocks via Leontief inverse

KEY TECHNICAL NOTES:
- I-O matrices ≠ Graph Laplacians (different mathematical properties)
- A matrices: Non-negative, row sums < 1, represent input coefficients
- L matrices: Diagonal > 1, represent total economic multipliers
- Graph Laplacians: Row sums = 0, off-diagonal ≤ 0, represent network structure
